4/10/24, 22:29 - Upasana C: from collections import defaultdict
import heapq

def findMinimumCost(tree_nodes, tree_from, tree_to, tree_weight, start, end):
    # Create a graph representation using adjacency list
    graph = defaultdict(list)
    for i in range(len(tree_from)):
        graph[tree_from[i]].append((tree_to[i], tree_weight[i]))
        graph[tree_to[i]].append((tree_from[i], tree_weight[i]))

    # Function to calculate the cost of traversing an edge for given count
    def edge_cost(weight, count):
        return weight * ((count // 2) + 1)

    # Function to find the minimum cost path using Dijkstra's algorithm
    def dijkstra():
        visited = set()
        pq = [(0, start, defaultdict(int))]
        while pq:
            cost, node, counts = heapq.heappop(pq)
            if node == end and all(counts.values()):
                return cost
            if node not in visited:
                visited.add(node)
                for neighbor, weight in graph[node]:
                    new_counts = counts.copy()
                    new_counts[neighbor] += 1
                    new_cost = cost + edge_cost(weight, new_counts[neighbor])
                    heapq.heappush(pq, (new_cost, neighbor, new_counts))
        return -1  # If there is no valid path
    
    return dijkstra()

# Example usage:
tree_from = [0, 0, 1, 1, 2, 2, 3, 4]
tree_to = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8]
tree_weight = [2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9]
start = 1
end = 4
minimum_cost = findMinimumCost(9, tree_from, tree_to, tree_weight, start, end)
print("Minimum cost:", minimum_cost)
4/10/24, 22:33 - Prachi Sah: def findMinimumCost(tree_nodes, tree_from, tree_to, tree_weight, start, end):
    adjList = {}
    for i in range(len(tree_from)):
        if tree_from[i] not in adjList:
            adjList[tree_from[i]] = []
        if tree_to[i] not in adjList:
            adjList[tree_to[i]] = []
        adjList[tree_from[i]].append((tree_to[i], tree_weight[i]))
        adjList[tree_to[i]].append((tree_from[i], tree_weight[i]))
    
    distance = [[math.inf] * (tree_nodes + 1) for _ in range(tree_nodes + 1)]
    distance[start][0] = 0
    pq = [(0, start, 0)]
    
    while pq:
        dist, u, visits = heapq.heappop(pq)
        
        if u == end and visits == tree_nodes:
            return dist
        
        if visits > tree_nodes:
            continue
        
        for neighbor in adjList.get(u, []):
            v, weight_uv = neighbor
            
            new_visits = visits + 1
            cost = weight_uv * math.ceil(new_visits / 2.0)
            
            if distance[v][new_visits] > dist + cost:
                distance[v][new_visits] = dist + cost
                heapq.heappush(pq, (distance[v][new_visits], v, new_visits))
    
    return -1

6/23/24, 09:51 - Prachi Sah: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>

using namespace std;

int countWays(int N, int K) {
    // Create a DP table where dp[n][k] represents the number of ways
    // to ensure the k-th chocolate is the last one remaining out of n chocolates.
    vector<vector<long long>> dp(N + 1, vector<long long>(N + 1, 0));

    // Base case: If there is only one chocolate, there's only one way, it's already the last one
    for (int k = 1; k <= N; ++k) {
        dp[1][k] = 1;
    }

    // Fill the DP table
    for (int n = 2; n <= N; ++n) {
        for (int k = 1; k <= n; ++k) {
            // If k-th chocolate is the last one remaining out of n chocolates,
            // it must avoid being removed in both directions
            // The k-th chocolate can be the last remaining if:
            // - The first chocolate is removed (then it's the same problem with (n-1) chocolates)
            // - The last chocolate is removed (then it's the same problem with (n-1) chocolates)
            dp[n][k] = dp[n-1][k];
            if (k > 1) {
                dp[n][k] += dp[n-1][k-1];
            }
            if (k < n) {
                dp[n][k] += dp[n-1][k+1];
            }
        }
    }

    // The answer is the number of ways to ensure the K-th chocolate is the last one remaining
    return dp[N][K];
}

int main() {
    int N, K;
    cout << "Enter the number of chocolates (N): ";
    cin >> N;
    cout << "Enter the position of the chocolate to be last (K): ";
    cin >> K;

    int result = countWays(N, K);
    cout << "Number of ways to ensure the " << K << "-th chocolate is the last one remaining: " << result << endl;

    return 0;
}

6/23/24, 09:58 - Vibha Chandola: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>

// Function to calculate the number of ways using dynamic programming
int countWays(int N, int K) {
    // Create a 2D DP table with (N+1)x(N+1) dimensions initialized to 0
    std::vector<std::vector<int>> dp(N + 1, std::vector<int>(N + 1, 0));

    // Base case: if there's only one chocolate, there's only one way
    for (int i = 1; i <= N; ++i) {
        dp[1][i] = 1;
    }

    // Fill the DP table
    for (int i = 2; i <= N; ++i) {
        for (int j = 1; j <= N; ++j) {
            if (j > 1) {
                dp[i][j] += dp[i - 1][j - 1]; // Taking the chocolate from the beginning
            }
            if (j < N) {
                dp[i][j] += dp[i - 1][j + 1]; // Taking the chocolate from the end
            }
        }
    }

    // The result is the number of ways to have K as the last chocolate remaining
    return dp[N][K];
}

int main() {
    int N, K;
    
    // Input the number of chocolates and the index of the last remaining chocolate
    std::cout << "Enter the number of chocolates (N): ";
    std::cin >> N;
    std::cout << "Enter the index of the last remaining chocolate (K): ";
    std::cin >> K;

    // Check if the inputs are within valid range
    if (N <= 0 || K <= 0 || K > N) {
        std::cerr << "Invalid input! N should be greater than 0 and K should be between 1 and N." << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }

    // Calculate the number of ways
    int result = countWays(N, K);

    // Output the result
    std::cout << "Number of possible ways: " << result << std::endl;

    return 0;
}

6/23/24, 09:59 - GuğŸ’©: def count_ways(N, K):
    def recurse(start, end, K):
        if start == end:
            return 1 if start == K else 0
        return recurse(start + 1, end, K) + recurse(start, end - 1, K)
    
    return recurse(1, N, K)

# Example usage
N = 5
K = 3
print(count_ways(N, K))  # Output will be the number of ways

6/23/24, 14:26 - Garima Kothari: def find_original_string(modified_string):
    vowels = {'a', 'e', 'o', 'u'}
 
    resulting_string = modified_string.replace('i', '')
    original_string = modified_string.replace(resulting_string, '', 1)
    if all(char in vowels for char in resulting_string) and all(char in vowels for char in original_string) and resulting_string != '' and original_string != '':
        return original_string
    else:
        return "notpossible"
original_string = find_original_string(modified_string)

6/23/24, 14:27 - Mokshita Joshi: #include <iostream>
#include <cmath>
using namespace std;

// Function to count commas used from 1 to N
int countCommas(int N) {
    int totalCommas = 0;
    int length = log10(N) + 1;  // Number of digits in N

    for (int digits = 4; digits <= length; ++digits) {
        // Calculate the lower and upper bounds for the current number of digits
        int lowerBound = pow(10, digits - 1);
        int upperBound = pow(10, digits) - 1;

        // Calculate the number of commas for numbers in this range
        int commasPerNumber = (digits - 1) / 3; // commas per number in this range

        // Handle the last range specially
        if (N < upperBound) {
            upperBound = N;
        }

        totalCommas += (upperBound - lowerBound + 1) * commasPerNumber;
    }

    return totalCommas;
}

int main() {
    int N;
    cout << "Enter the value of N: ";
    cin >> N;
    cout << "Total commas used: " << countCommas(N) << endl;
    return 0;
}

6/23/24, 19:10 - Mokshita Joshi: def count_bounty_numbers(N):
    MOD = 10007
    
    if N == 1:
        return 0
    
    total_N_digit_numbers = 9 * (10 ** (N - 1)) % MOD
    no_zero_numbers = 9 ** N % MOD
    one_zero_numbers = (N - 1) * (9 ** (N - 1)) % MOD
    
    at_least_two_zeros = (total_N_digit_numbers - no_zero_numbers - one_zero_numbers) % MOD
    
    return at_least_two_zeros

# Example usage:

6/23/24, 19:11 - Garima Kothari: def count_disqualified_players(player_records, k):
    player_ball_count = {}
    disqualified_players = set()

    for player_id, ball_number in player_records:
        if player_id not in player_ball_count:
            player_ball_count[player_id] = {}
        
        if ball_number not in player_ball_count[player_id]:
            player_ball_count[player_id][ball_number] = 1
        else:
            player_ball_count[player_id][ball_number] += 1

        if player_ball_count[player_id][ball_number] > k:
            disqualified_players.add(player_id)

    return len(disqualified_players)

6/23/24, 19:28 - Divanshi C: class Solution {
public:
    int bounty(int input1) {
        int n = input1;
        const int m = 10007;

        if (n < 2) {
            return 0;
        }

        long long t = (9 * pow(10, n - 1, m)) % m;
        long long num = pow(9, n, m);
        long long na = ((n - 1) * pow(9, n - 1, m)) % m;
        long long res = (t - num - na) % m;

        // Ensure res is non-negative
        if (res < 0) {
            res += m;
        }

        return res;
    }

private:
    long long pow(long long base, long long exp, int mod) {
        long long result = 1;
        while (exp > 0) {
            if (exp % 2 == 1) {
                result = (result * base) % mod;
            }
            base = (base * base) % mod;
            exp /= 2;
        }
        return result;
    }
};

int fact(int n)
{
    if (n == 0 || n == 1)
        return 1;
    else
        return n * fact(n - 1);
}

int bounty(int input1)
{
    int n = input1;
    if (n < 2)
    {
        return 0;
    }
    if (n == 2)
    {
        return 1;
    }
    long long res1 = 9;
    for (int i = 1; i <= n - 3; i++)
    {
        res1 = (res1 * 10) % mod;
    }
    int res2 = fact(n - 1);
    int res3 = fact(2);
    int res4 = res2 / res3;
    res4 = res4 % mod;
    res1 = (res1 * res4) % mod;
    return res1;
}

using namespace std;

int count_bounty_numbers(int N) {
    const int MOD = 10007;

    if (N < 3) {
        return 0;
    }

    long long total_numbers = 9 * pow(10, N-1);
    long long no_zero_numbers = pow(9, N);
    long long one_zero_numbers = (N-1) * pow(9, N-1);

    long long result = (total_numbers - no_zero_numbers - one_zero_numbers) % MOD;

    return result;
}

int main() {
    int N;
    cout << "Enter the number of digits (N): ";
    cin >> N;

    int result = count_bounty_numbers(N);
    cout << result << endl;

    return 0;
}

int binPow(int a, int b, int mod)
{
    int res = 1;
    while (b)
    {
        if (b & 1)
        {
            res = (res * a) % mod;
        }
        a = (a * a) % mod;
        b = b >> 1;
    }
    return res;
}

6/23/24, 20:07 - Upasana C: int playerDisqualified(int input1,int input2, int **input3)
{
    int ans = 0;
    int n = input1;
    int k = input2;


    map<pair<int,int>,int> mm;
    map<int,int> mp;
    map<int,int> ds;

    for(int i=0;i<n;i++){
        mp[input3[i][0]]++;
        pair<int,int> p;
        p.first = input3[i][0];
        p.second = input3[i][1];

        mm[p]++;
        if(mm[p] >= k){
            ds[input3[i][0]]++;
        }
    }

    return mp.size() - ds.size();
}

    from collections import defaultdict
    
    player_ball_count = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(int))
    disqualified_players = set()

6/23/24, 20:22 - Upasana C: import java.util.HashMap;
import java.util.Map;

class Solution {
    public int playerDisqualification(int N, int K, int[][] input) {

        Map<Integer, Map<Integer, Integer>> ballCounts = new HashMap<>();

     
            int playerId = input[i][0];
            int ballNumber = input[i][1];

            
            if (!ballCounts.containsKey(playerId)) {
                ballCounts.put(playerId, new HashMap<>());
            }

         
            Map<Integer, Integer> playerBallCounts = ballCounts.get(playerId);
            playerBallCounts.put(ballNumber, playerBallCounts.getOrDefault(ballNumber, 0) + 1);
        }

    
        int disqualifiedPlayers = 0;
        for (Map<Integer, Integer> playerBallCounts : ballCounts.values()) {
            for (int count : playerBallCounts.values()) {
                if (count > K) {
                    disqualifiedPlayers++;
                    break;
                }
            }
        }

        return disqualifiedPlayers;
    }
}
6/23/24, 20:24 - Mokshita Joshi: from collections import defaultdict

def player_disqualification(n, k, input):
    cnt = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(int))

    for i in range(n):
        pid = input[i][0]
        bnum = input[i][1]
        cnt[pid][bnum] += 1

    dq = 0
    for p in cnt:
        disq = False
        for b in cnt[p]:
            if cnt[p][b] > k:
                disq = True
                break
        if disq:
            dq += 1

    return dq

# Example usage:
n = 7
k = 2
input_data = [
    [1, 10],
    [1, 10],
    [1, 10],
    [2, 20],
    [2, 20],
    [3, 20],
    [3, 20],
]

print(player_disqualification(n, k, input_data))  # Output should be 1

7/21/24, 11:38 - Divanshi C: class Solution {
public:
    int longestValidParentheses(string s) {
        stack<int> st;
        st.push(-1);
        int max_len = 0;

        for (int i = 0; i < s.length(); i++) {
            if (s[i] == '(') {
                st.push(i);
            } else {
                st.pop();
                if (st.empty()) {
                    st.push(i);
                } else {
                    max_len = max(max_len, i - st.top());
                }
            }
        }

        return max_len;        
    }
};

7/21/24, 12:06 - Garima Kothari: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <unordered_set>

using namespace std;

int longestUniqueSequence(int n, vector<int>& songs) {
    unordered_set<int> song_set;
    int start = 0, max_length = 0;

    for (int end = 0; end < n; ++end) {
        while (song_set.find(songs[end]) != song_set.end()) {
            song_set.erase(songs[start]);
            ++start;
        }
        song_set.insert(songs[end]);
        max_length = max(max_length, end - start + 1);
    }

    return max_length;
}

int main() {
    int n;
    cin >> n;
    vector<int> songs(n);
    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        cin >> songs[i];
    }

    cout << longestUniqueSequence(n, songs) << endl;

    return 0;
}

7/21/24, 12:06 - Divanshi C: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <unordered_set>

using namespace std;

int longestUniqueSongSequence(int n, const vector<int>& songs) {
    unordered_set<int> seen;
    int start = 0, max_length = 0;

    for (int end = 0; end < n; ++end) {
        while (seen.find(songs[end]) != seen.end()) {
            seen.erase(songs[start]);
            ++start;
        }
        seen.insert(songs[end]);
        max_length = max(max_length, end - start + 1);
    }

    return max_length;
}

int main() {
    int n;
    cin >> n;

    vector<int> songs(n);
    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        cin >> songs[i];
    }

    int result = longestUniqueSongSequence(n, songs);

    cout << result << endl;

    return 0;
}

7/27/24, 11:59 - Priyanka Kandpal: class Solution {
public:

    // 3[a]2[bc] 
    string helper(int &idx, string str){
        int n=0;
        string ans="";

        while(idx<str.size()){
            char curr=str[idx];
            if(curr>='0' && curr <='9'){
                n= n*10 + curr- '0';
            }
            else if( curr=='['){
                string temp=helper(++idx, str);
                // while(str[idx]!=']'){
                //     temp+= str[idx];
                //     idx++;
                // }
                while(n>0){
                    ans+= temp;
                    n--;
                }
            }
            else if(curr==']'){
                return ans;
            }
            else{
                ans+=curr;
            }
            idx++;
        }
        return ans;
        
    }
    string decodeString(string s) {
        int i=0;
        return helper(i,s);
    }
};

7/27/24, 12:01 - Priyanka Kandpal: class Solution {
public:
    int calculate(string s) {
        long long int sum = 0;
        int sign = 1;
        stack<pair<int,int>> st;

        for(int i=0; i<s.size();i++){
            if(isdigit(s[i])){
                long long int num = 0;
                while(i<s.size() && isdigit(s[i])){
                    num = num * 10 + (s[i] - '0');
                    i++;
                }
                i--;
                sum += num * sign;
                sign = 1;
            }
            else if(s[i] == '('){
                st.push({sum, sign});
                sum = 0;
                sign = 1;
            }
            else if(s[i] == ')'){
                sum = st.top().first + (st.top().second * sum);
                st.pop();

            }
            else if(s[i] == '-'){
                sign = -1 * sign;
            }
        }
        return sum;
    }
};

7/27/24, 12:37 - Vibha Chandola: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <string>

std::vector<int> findPeriods(const std::string &s) {
    int n = s.length();
    std::vector<int> pi(n, 0);
    std::vector<int> periods;

    for (int i = 1; i < n; ++i) {
        int j = pi[i - 1];
        while (j > 0 && s[i] != s[j]) {
            j = pi[j - 1];
        }
        if (s[i] == s[j]) {
            ++j;
        }
        pi[i] = j;
    }

    int len = n;
    while (len > 0) {
        periods.push_back(len);
        len = pi[len - 1];
    }

    std::reverse(periods.begin(), periods.end());
    return periods;
}

int main() {
    std::string s;
    std::cin >> s;

    std::vector<int> periods = findPeriods(s);

    for (int period : periods) {
        std::cout << period << " ";
    }

    std::cout << std::endl;
    return 0;
}

7/27/24, 12:38 - Vibha Chandola: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <string>

using namespace std;

// Function to compute the prefix function for the string
vector<int> computePrefixFunction(const string &s) {
    int n = s.length();
    vector<int> pi(n);
    for (int i = 1; i < n; ++i) {
        int j = pi[i - 1];
        while (j > 0 && s[i] != s[j])
            j = pi[j - 1];
        if (s[i] == s[j])
            ++j;
        pi[i] = j;
    }
    return pi;
}

// Function to find all period lengths of the string
vector<int> findPeriodLengths(const string &s) {
    int n = s.length();
    vector<int> pi = computePrefixFunction(s);
    vector<int> periods;
    
    for (int i = 1; i <= n; ++i) {
        if (n % i == 0 && pi[n - 1] % i == 0) {
            periods.push_back(i);
        }
    }
    return periods;
}

int main() {
    string s;
    cin >> s;

    vector<int> periods = findPeriodLengths(s);
    
    for (int period : periods) {
        cout << period << " ";
    }
    cout << endl;

    return 0;
}

8/6/24, 16:32 - GuğŸ’©: If you need to detect a cycle in a graph quickly using C++, you can use Depth-First Search (DFS). Here's a very short example of how you might implement cycle detection in a graph:

```cpp
#include <iostream>
#include <vector>

using namespace std;

bool dfs(int node, vector<vector<int>>& adj, vector<bool>& visited, vector<bool>& recStack) {
    visited[node] = true;
    recStack[node] = true;

    for (int neighbor : adj[node]) {
        if (!visited[neighbor] && dfs(neighbor, adj, visited, recStack)) {
            return true;
        } else if (recStack[neighbor]) {
            return true;
        }
    }

    recStack[node] = false;
    return false;
}

bool detectCycle(int V, vector<vector<int>>& adj) {
    vector<bool> visited(V, false);
    vector<bool> recStack(V, false);

    for (int i = 0; i < V; i++) {
        if (!visited[i]) {
            if (dfs(i, adj, visited, recStack)) {
                return true;
            }
        }
    }

    return false;
}

int main() {
    int V = 4;
    vector<vector<int>> adj(V);

    // Example edges for testing
    adj[0].push_back(1);
    adj[1].push_back(2);
    adj[2].push_back(3);
    adj[3].push_back(1); // This creates a cycle

    if (detectCycle(V, adj)) {
        cout << "Cycle detected" << endl;
    } else {
        cout << "No cycle detected" << endl;
    }

    return 0;
}
```

In this example:

- `adj` is an adjacency list representing the graph.
- `dfs` is a recursive function that uses a stack to keep track of the nodes currently in the recursion stack.
- `detectCycle` initializes visited and recursion stack vectors and calls `dfs` to check for cycles in each component of the graph.

Adjust the number of vertices (`V`) and edges in the `main` function according to your graph structure.

8/20/24, 23:46 - Divanshi C: ### 1. What is a Database Management System (DBMS)? Explain its significance in comparison to a traditional file processing system.

A **Database Management System (DBMS)** is a software system that allows users to define, create, maintain, and control access to a database. A DBMS provides a systematic way of organizing, storing, and retrieving data from a database. It offers functionalities such as data security, data integrity, and data backup, which are crucial for managing large volumes of data efficiently.

**Significance in comparison to traditional file processing systems:**
- **Data Redundancy and Inconsistency:** Traditional file processing systems often suffer from data redundancy (duplicate data) and data inconsistency (conflicting data). A DBMS minimizes redundancy and ensures data consistency by centralizing data storage and managing it in a controlled environment.
- **Data Integrity:** In file processing systems, maintaining data integrity is difficult due to the lack of constraints. DBMS enforces data integrity through constraints and rules, ensuring data accuracy and consistency.
- **Data Security:** DBMS provides advanced security features like user authentication, access control, and encryption, which are not available in traditional file systems.
- **Concurrent Access:** In a traditional file system, concurrent access to data by multiple users can lead to conflicts. DBMS allows multiple users to access the data simultaneously while ensuring data consistency through transaction management.
- **Data Independence:** DBMS supports data independence, allowing changes in the database structure without affecting the application programs, whereas file processing systems lack this feature.

### 2. Discuss the main advantages of using a DBMS over a file processing system. Provide examples to support your answer.

**Advantages of using a DBMS over a file processing system:**

1. **Reduced Data Redundancy and Inconsistency:**
   - Example: In a university system, student data may be stored in multiple files (e.g., admission records, exam records). Using a DBMS, data is stored centrally, reducing redundancy and ensuring consistency across all departments.

2. **Improved Data Integrity and Accuracy:**
   - Example: A DBMS can enforce rules such as primary key constraints, ensuring that each record is unique and accurate. In a payroll system, this prevents duplicate employee records.

3. **Enhanced Data Security:**
   - Example: In a banking system, a DBMS can restrict access to sensitive data like account balances, ensuring only authorized users can access or modify this information.

4. **Efficient Data Access and Querying:**
   - Example: A DBMS allows complex queries to be executed quickly, such as finding all customers who made purchases over $1,000 last month. In a file system, this would require manually searching through records.

5. **Better Data Backup and Recovery:**
   - Example: A DBMS can automatically back up data and recover it in case of failure, ensuring minimal data loss. A file processing system requires manual backups, which can be error-prone.

6. **Support for Concurrent Access:**
   - Example: In an online shopping system, multiple users can access the product catalog and place orders simultaneously without conflicts, thanks to DBMS transaction management.

### 3. Explain the concept of data abstraction in DBMS. How does it help in managing data complexity?

**Data abstraction** in DBMS refers to the process of hiding the complexity of data storage and representation from the users and providing a simplified view of the data. It involves three levels:

1. **Physical Level (Lowest Level):** Describes how data is actually stored in the database, including file structures and storage details.
2. **Logical Level (Middle Level):** Describes what data is stored in the database and the relationships between the data. This level hides the physical storage details and provides a logical view of the data.
3. **View Level (Highest Level):** Describes only a part of the entire database, relevant to the user. Different users can have different views of the same data based on their needs.

**How it helps in managing data complexity:**
- **Simplification for Users:** Users interact with the view level, which simplifies their interaction with the data, as they do not need to understand the underlying complexities.
- **Data Independence:** By separating the physical and logical levels, changes in data storage do not affect application programs, allowing for flexibility and easier maintenance.
- **Efficient Data Management:** Data abstraction allows database administrators to optimize physical storage without affecting user interaction with the data.

### 4. What are the different types of data independence in DBMS? Explain the importance of each.

**Data Independence** refers to the ability to change the database schema at one level without affecting the schema at the next higher level. There are two types of data independence:

1. **Logical Data Independence:**
   - **Definition:** The ability to change the logical schema (e.g., adding or deleting tables or changing relationships) without affecting the external schema or application programs.
   - **Importance:** It allows developers to change the logical structure of the database, such as restructuring or reorganizing data, without requiring changes to the user interface or application programs. This flexibility is crucial for adapting to evolving business requirements.

2. **Physical Data Independence:**
   - **Definition:** The ability to change the physical schema (e.g., how data is stored on disk) without affecting the logical schema or application programs.
   - **Importance:** It enables database administrators to optimize performance by modifying storage structures, indexing strategies, or hardware configurations without impacting the logical view of the data or the applications that use it.

### 5. Describe the various database languages used in DBMS. What is the purpose of each language?

**Database languages** in DBMS are used to interact with the database. The primary languages include:

1. **Data Definition Language (DDL):**
   - **Purpose:** Used to define and modify the database schema, including creating, altering, and dropping tables, indexes, and constraints.
   - **Example:** `CREATE TABLE`, `ALTER TABLE`, `DROP TABLE`.

2. **Data Manipulation Language (DML):**
   - **Purpose:** Used to retrieve, insert, update, and delete data in the database.
   - **Example:** `SELECT`, `INSERT`, `UPDATE`, `DELETE`.

3. **Data Control Language (DCL):**
   - **Purpose:** Used to control access to data in the database by granting and revoking permissions to users.
   - **Example:** `GRANT`, `REVOKE`.

4. **Transaction Control Language (TCL):**
   - **Purpose:** Used to manage transactions in the database, ensuring data integrity and consistency.
   - **Example:** `COMMIT`, `ROLLBACK`, `SAVEPOINT`.

5. **Query Language (QL):**
   - **Purpose:** Used to query and retrieve data from the database. SQL (Structured Query Language) is the most commonly used query language.
   - **Example:** `SELECT * FROM Customers WHERE Age > 30`.

### 6. List and describe the primary components of a DBMS. How do these components interact to manage a database?

The primary components of a DBMS include:

1. **Database Engine:**
   - **Description:** The core service for accessing and processing data. It manages data storage, query processing, and transaction management.
   - **Interaction:** Executes database operations like insertions, updates, and retrievals. It interacts with storage management to access data and the query processor to execute user queries.

2. **Database Schema:**
   - **Description:** Defines the logical structure of the data, including tables, fields, relationships, and constraints.
   - **Interaction:** Provides the blueprint for organizing and accessing data in the database.

3. **Query Processor:**
   - **Description:** Translates user queries into executable commands for the database engine.
   - **Interaction:** Converts high-level queries (e.g., SQL) into low-level instructions that the database engine can execute.

4. **Storage Manager:**
   - **Description:** Manages the physical storage of data on disk, including data files, indexes, and metadata.
   - **Interaction:** Handles data storage and retrieval, working closely with the database engine to provide data access.

5. **Transaction Manager:**
   - **Description:** Ensures that database transactions are executed properly, maintaining data integrity and consistency.
   - **Interaction:** Coordinates with the database engine to ensure that transactions follow ACID (Atomicity, Consistency, Isolation, Durability) properties.

6. **Metadata Manager:**
   - **Description:** Manages metadata (data about data), such as schema definitions and data constraints.
   - **Interaction:** Provides information to the query processor and database engine about the structure and rules of the database.

7. **User Interface:**
   - **Description:** Provides a way for users to interact with the database, often through a graphical user interface (GUI) or command-line interface (CLI).
   - **Interaction:** Allows users to submit queries, view results, and perform database management tasks.

### 7. Illustrate the overall structure of a DBMS with a diagram and brief explanation of each component.

**Diagram:**
```
+-------------------------------------+
|             User Interface          |
+-------------------------------------+
               |
               v
+-------------------------------------+
|            Query Processor          |
+-------------------------------------+
               |
               v
+-------------------------------------+
|          Transaction Manager        |
+-------------------------------------+
               |
               v
+-------------------------------------+
|           Database Engine           |
+-------------------------------------+
|   |                       |         |
| Storage Manager     Metadata Manager|
+-------------------------------------+
               |
               v
+-------------------------------------+
|             Physical Storage        |
+-------------------------------------+
```

**Explanation of each component:**
- **User Interface:** Allows users to interact with the DBMS.
- **Query Processor:** Translates user queries into commands for the database engine.
- **Transaction Manager:** Manages transactions to ensure data integrity.
- **Database Engine:** Executes database operations and manages data

9/21/24, 20:06 - Divanshi C: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <cmath>  // For pow function

using namespace std;

// Function to calculate the product of ordinal values raised to power m
long long calculateValue(const string &str, int m) {
    long long value = 1;
    for (char ch : str) {
        int ordValue = static_cast<int>(ch);  // Get ordinal value (ASCII)
        value *= pow(ordValue, m);            // Raise to the power of m
    }
    return value;
}

int main() {
    vector<string> s = {"abc", "abcd"};  // Example strings
    int m = 2;  // Example power
    long long totalSum = 0;
    
    // Loop over each string in the array
    for (const string &str : s) {
        totalSum += calculateValue(str, m);  // Sum up the values of each string
    }
    
    // Check if the sum is even or odd
    if (totalSum % 2 == 0) {
        cout << "EVEN" << endl;
    } else {
        cout << "ODD" << endl;
    }

    return 0;
}

9/21/24, 20:19 - Manvi Joshi: class Solution:
    def minIncrementForUnique(self, nums: List[int]) -> int:
        if not nums:
            return 0
        
        nums.sort()
        moves = 0
        prev = nums[0]
        
        for i in range(1, len(nums)):
            if nums[i] <= prev:
                prev += 1
                moves += prev - nums[i]
            else:
                prev = nums[i]
        
        return moves

9/21/24, 20:24 - Manvi Joshi: class Solution {
public:
    int minIncrementForUnique(vector<int>& nums) {
        sort(nums.begin(),nums.end());
        int largest = INT_MIN;
        int res = 0;
        for(int i=0; i<nums.size(); i++){
            if(nums[i] > largest){
                largest = nums[i];
            }else{
                res += largest-nums[i]+1;
                largest++;
            }
        }
        return res;
    }
};

9/21/24, 20:27 - Manvi Joshi: def min_cost_to_make_distinct(pods, cost):
    n = len(pods)
    # Zip pods and cost together and sort based on the pod values
    pods_costs = sorted(zip(pods, cost), key=lambda x: x[0])
    
    total_cost = 0
    
    # Traverse through the sorted list and fix duplicates
    for i in range(1, n):
        prev_pod, prev_cost = pods_costs[i-1]
        curr_pod, curr_cost = pods_costs[i]
        
        if curr_pod <= prev_pod:  # If current pod is not greater than the previous one
            diff = prev_pod - curr_pod + 1  # Find how much we need to increment
            total_cost += diff * curr_cost  # Add the cost of incrementing
            pods_costs[i] = (curr_pod + diff, curr_cost)  # Update the current pod count
    
    return total_cost

# Example usage
pods = [5, 2, 5, 3, 3]
cost = [13, 7, 8, 6, 9]
print(min_cost_to_make_distinct(pods, cost))  # Output: 17

9/21/24, 20:28 - Manvi Joshi: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <algorithm>
using namespace std;

int min_cost_to_make_distinct(vector<int>& pods, vector<int>& cost) {
    int n = pods.size();
    // Zip pods and cost together and sort based on pod values
    vector<pair<int, int>> pods_costs;
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
        pods_costs.push_back({pods[i], cost[i]});
    }
    sort(pods_costs.begin(), pods_costs.end());

    int total_cost = 0;

    // Traverse through the sorted list and fix duplicates
    for (int i = 1; i < n; i++) {
        int prev_pod = pods_costs[i - 1].first;
        int curr_pod = pods_costs[i].first;
        int curr_cost = pods_costs[i].second;

        if (curr_pod <= prev_pod) {  // If current pod is not greater than the previous one
            int diff = prev_pod - curr_pod + 1;  // Find how much we need to increment
            total_cost += diff * curr_cost;  // Add the cost of incrementing
            pods_costs[i].first += diff;  // Update the current pod count
        }
    }

    return total_cost;
}

int main() {
    vector<int> pods = {5, 2, 5, 3, 3};
    vector<int> cost = {13, 7, 8, 6, 9};

    cout << min_cost_to_make_distinct(pods, cost) << endl;  // Output: 17
    return 0;
}

9/21/24, 20:30 - Prachi Sah: #include <vector>
#include <string>
using namespace std;

// Function to calculate power manually
long long power(int base, int exp) {
    long long result = 1;
    for (int i = 0; i < exp; ++i) {
        result *= base;
    }
    return result;
}

string solve(int m, const vector<string>& s) {
    long long total = 0;

    for (const string& str : s) {
        long long val = 1;

        // Calculate the value for each string
        for (char ch : str) {
            val *= power(static_cast<int>(ch), m);  // Use manual power function
        }

        total += val;
    }

    // Check if the total sum is EVEN or ODD
    return (total % 2 == 0) ? "EVEN" : "ODD";
}

9/21/24, 21:35 - AnağŸ¤: def min_swap_cost(arrA, arrB):
    # Sort both arrays in descending order
    arrA.sort(reverse=True)
    arrB.sort(reverse=True)

    # Check if they can be made equal by comparing sorted versions
    if sorted(arrA) != sorted(arrB):
        return -1
    
    # Pointers for mismatches
    i, j = 0, 0
    n = len(arrA)
    total_cost = 0

    # Traverse both arrays
    while i < n and j < n:
        # If elements are equal, move both pointers
        if arrA[i] == arrB[j]:
            i += 1
            j += 1
        # If element in arrA is larger, move arrA pointer to find a swap candidate
        elif arrA[i] > arrB[j]:
            i += 1
        # If element in arrB is larger, move arrB pointer to find a swap candidate
        else:
            j += 1
    
    # Identify excess elements in arrA and arrB separately
    # This is necessary for calculating the swap cost
    excess_A = []
    excess_B = []
    
    i, j = 0, 0
    while i < n or j < n:
        if i < n and (j >= n or arrA[i] > arrB[j]):
            excess_A.append(arrA[i])
            i += 1
        elif j < n and (i >= n or arrB[j] > arrA[i]):
            excess_B.append(arrB[j])
            j += 1
        else:
            i += 1
            j += 1
    
    # The number of excess elements must be the same in both arrays
    if len(excess_A) != len(excess_B):
        return -1
    
    # Sort excess arrays for optimal swap matching
    excess_A.sort()
    excess_B.sort()

    # Calculate total minimum cost for swapping mismatches
    for i in range(len(excess_A)):
        total_cost += min(excess_A[i], excess_B[i])

    return total_cost

# Example Usage
arrA = [4, 2, 2, 2]
arrB = [1, 4, 1, 2]
print(min_swap_cost(arrA, arrB))  # Output: 3

*Pods and Costs*

// question 3: pods and cost

#include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <algorithm>
#include <set>

using namespace std;
int getMinCost(vector<int>& pods, vector<int>& cost) {
    vector<pair<int, int>> pp;
    
    for (int i = 0; i < pods.size(); i++) {
        pp.push_back({pods[i], cost[i]});
    }
    
    sort(pp.begin(), pp.end());
    int ans = 0;
    for (int i = 0; i < pods.size() - 1; i++) {
        if (pp[i].first == pp[i + 1].first) 
            ans += min(pp[i].second, pp[i + 1].second);
    }
    return ans;
}

int main() {
    vector<int> pods = {5, 2, 5, 3, 3};
    vector<int> cost = {3, 7, 8, 6, 9};

    cout << getMinCost(pods, cost);
    
    return 0;
}

*// Atlassian Test collab tool* 

#include <bits/stdc++.h>

using namespace std;

string ltrim(const string &);
string rtrim(const string &);
vector<string> split(const string &);

string solve(int m, vector<string> s) {
    // fill this function
    int n = s.size(); 
    vector<int> v(n , 1); 
    
    for(int i = 0 ;i < n ; i++){
        
        for(auto it : s[i]){
            if( (it - 'a' + 97 )%2 == 0){
                v[i] = 0 ; 
                break; 
            }
        }
       
    }
    
    // if(v[n-1]==1)return "EVEN";
    
    
    int sum = 0 ; 
    for(auto it : v) sum += it ;
    
    if((sum) %2 ==1) return "ODD";
    return "EVEN"; 

}

int main()
{
    ofstream fout(getenv("OUTPUT_PATH"));

    string t_temp;
    getline(cin, t_temp);

    int t = stoi(ltrim(rtrim(t_temp)));

    for (int t_itr = 0; t_itr < t; t_itr++) {
        string first_multiple_input_temp;
        getline(cin, first_multiple_input_temp);

        vector<string> first_multiple_input = split(rtrim(first_multiple_input_temp));

        int m = stoi(first_multiple_input[0]);

        int k = stoi(first_multiple_input[1]);

        string s_temp_temp;
        getline(cin, s_temp_temp);

        vector<string> s_temp = split(rtrim(s_temp_temp));

        vector<string> s(k);

        for (int i = 0; i < k; i++) {
            string s_item = s_temp[i];

            s[i] = s_item;
        }

        string ans = solve(m, s);

        fout << ans << "\n";
    }

    fout.close();

    return 0;
}

string ltrim(const string &str) {
    string s(str);

    s.erase(
        s.begin(),
        find_if(s.begin(), s.end(), not1(ptr_fun<int, int>(isspace)))
    );

    return s;
}

string rtrim(const string &str) {
    string s(str);

    s.erase(
        find_if(s.rbegin(), s.rend(), not1(ptr_fun<int, int>(isspace))).base(),
        s.end()
    );

    return s;
}

vector<string> split(const string &str) {
    vector<string> tokens;

    string::size_type start = 0;
    string::size_type end = 0;

    while ((end = str.find(" ", start)) != string::npos) {
        tokens.push_back(str.substr(start, end - start));

        start = end + 1;
    }

    tokens.push_back(str.substr(start));

    return tokens;
}

10/6/24, 11:47 - GuğŸ’©: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <algorithm>
#include <numeric>

using namespace std;

// Helper function to check if a given maximum length per day is feasible
bool canDivide(const vector<int>& trails, int days, int maxLength) {
    int currentSum = 0;
    int requiredDays = 1;
    
    for (int trail : trails) {
        if (currentSum + trail > maxLength) {
            // Start a new day
            requiredDays++;
            currentSum = trail;
            if (requiredDays > days) {
                return false;  // Too many days required
            }
        } else {
            currentSum += trail;
        }
    }
    
    return true;
}

int efficientTrek(vector<int>& trails, int record) {
    // Binary search over possible maximum trail lengths
    int left = *max_element(trails.begin(), trails.end());  // The longest single trail
    int right = accumulate(trails.begin(), trails.end(), 0);  // Sum of all trail lengths
    int result = right;
    
    while (left <= right) {
        int mid = left + (right - left) / 2;
        
        if (canDivide(trails, record, mid)) {
            result = mid;  // It's feasible, so try for a smaller maximum
            right = mid - 1;
        } else {
            left = mid + 1;  // It's not feasible, try a larger maximum
        }
    }
    
    return result;
}

int main() {
    vector<int> trails = {10, 5, 9, 3, 8, 15};
    int record = 2;
    
    cout << "Minimum sum of longest trails per day: " << efficientTrek(trails, record) << endl;
    
    return 0;
}

10/6/24, 11:49 - Prachi Sah: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <algorithm>

using namespace std;

int sumOfRegions(const vector<int>& heights) {
    int totalSum = 0;
    int n = heights.size();

    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        int left = i;
        int right = i;

        while (left > 0 && heights[left - 1] < heights[i]) {
            left--;
        }
        
        while (right < n - 1 && heights[right + 1] <= heights[i]) {
            right++;
        }

        int regionLength = right - left + 1;
        totalSum += regionLength;
    }

    return totalSum;
}

int main() {
    vector<int> heights = {3, 5, 6};
    int result = sumOfRegions(heights);
    cout << "Sum of regions: " << result << endl;
    return 0;
}

10/6/24, 11:52 - Prachi Sah: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <algorithm>
#include <numeric>

using namespace std;

pair<int, int> findWeightedMedian(const vector<int>& x, const vector<int>& y, const vector<int>& premium) {
    int n = x.size();
    vector<pair<int, int>> xCoord(n), yCoord(n);
    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        xCoord[i] = {x[i], premium[i]};
        yCoord[i] = {y[i], premium[i]};
    }
    
    sort(xCoord.begin(), xCoord.end());
    sort(yCoord.begin(), yCoord.end());

    auto getWeightedMedian = [](const vector<pair<int, int>>& coords) {
        int totalWeight = 0;
        for (const auto& [coord, weight] : coords) {
            totalWeight += weight;
        }
        
        int halfWeight = totalWeight / 2;
        int cumulativeWeight = 0;
        
        for (const auto& [coord, weight] : coords) {
            cumulativeWeight += weight;
            if (cumulativeWeight >= halfWeight) {
                return coord;
            }
        }
        
        return -1;
    };

    int optimalCx = getWeightedMedian(xCoord);
    int optimalCy = getWeightedMedian(yCoord);
    
    return {optimalCx, optimalCy};
}

int calculateCost(int cx, int cy, const vector<int>& x, const vector<int>& y, const vector<int>& premium) {
    int totalCost = 0;
    for (int i = 0; i < x.size(); ++i) {
        int distance = abs(x[i] - cx) + abs(y[i] - cy);
        totalCost += premium[i] * distance;
    }
    return totalCost;
}

int main() {
    vector<int> x = {1, 3, 2, 4};
    vector<int> y = {1, 2, 3, 4};
    vector<int> premium = {1, 3, 2, 4};

    auto [optimalCx, optimalCy] = findWeightedMedian(x, y, premium);
    int minCost = calculateCost(optimalCx, optimalCy, x, y, premium);
    
    cout << "Optimal location: (" << optimalCx << ", " << optimalCy << ")" << endl;
    cout << "Minimum cost to connect the control center: " << minCost << endl;

    return 0;
}
10/6/24, 11:54 - GuğŸ’©: Dual core:

vector<long long> getProcessTime(vector<int>& time) {
    int n = time.size();
    
    reverse(time.begin(), time.end());
    
    vector<long long> dp(n, 0);
    long long tot = 0;

    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        tot += time[i];
        if (i == 0) {
            dp[i] = tot;
        } else {
            dp[i] = max(dp[i - 1], tot - dp[i - 1]);
        }
    }

    vector<long long> ans = {dp[n - 1], tot - dp[n - 1]};
    return ans;
}
10/6/24, 11:55 - Vibha Chandola: *straight line region:*

long long calculateTotalRegion(vector<int>& heights) {
    int n = heights.size();
    vector<int> left_p(n), right_p(n);
    stack<int> st;

    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        while (!st.empty() && heights[st.top()] <= heights[i]) {
            st.pop();
        }
        left_p[i] = st.empty() ? 0 : st.top() + 1;
        st.push(i);
    }

    while (!st.empty()) st.pop();

    for (int i = n - 1; i >= 0; --i) {
        while (!st.empty() && heights[st.top()] <= heights[i]) {
            st.pop();
        }
        right_p[i] = st.empty() ? n - 1 : st.top() - 1;
        st.push(i);
    }

    long long totalRegion = 0;
    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        totalRegion += (right_p[i] - left_p[i] + 1);
    }

    return totalRegion;
}
10/6/24, 11:55 - GuğŸ’©: *straight line region:*

long long calculateTotalRegion(vector<int>& heights) {
    int n = heights.size();
    vector<int> left_p(n), right_p(n);
    stack<int> st;

    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        while (!st.empty() && heights[st.top()] <= heights[i]) {
            st.pop();
        }
        left_p[i] = st.empty() ? 0 : st.top() + 1;
        st.push(i);
    }

    while (!st.empty()) st.pop();

    for (int i = n - 1; i >= 0; --i) {
        while (!st.empty() && heights[st.top()] <= heights[i]) {
            st.pop();
        }
        right_p[i] = st.empty() ? n - 1 : st.top() - 1;
        st.push(i);
    }

    long long totalRegion = 0;
    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        totalRegion += (right_p[i] - left_p[i] + 1);
    }

    return totalRegion;
}

10/6/24, 12:08 - GuğŸ’©: int windFarms(vector<int> premium, vector<int> x, vector<int> y) {
    int n = premium.size();
    vector<pair<int, int>> x_premium, y_premium;

    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        x_premium.push_back({x[i], premium[i]});
        y_premium.push_back({y[i], premium[i]});
    }

    auto f = [&](vector<pair<int, int>>& coord_premium) {
        int total_weight = 0;
        for (const auto& cp : coord_premium) {
            total_weight += cp.second;
        }

        int sum = 0;
        for (const auto& cp : coord_premium) {
            sum += cp.second;
            if (sum >= (total_weight + 1) / 2) {
                return cp.first;
            }
        }
        return 0;
    };

    sort(x_premium.begin(), x_premium.end());
    sort(y_premium.begin(), y_premium.end());

    int cx = f(x_premium);
    int cy = f(y_premium);

    int total_cost = 0;
    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
        total_cost += premium[i] * (abs(x[i] - cx) + abs(y[i] - cy));
    }

    return total_cost;
}

10/6/24, 12:14 - GuğŸ’©: int efficientTrek(vector<int>& trails, int record) {
    int n = trails.size();
    vector<vector<int>> dp(n + 1, vector<int>(record + 1, INT_MAX));
    dp[0][0] = 0;

    for (int j = 1; j <= record; ++j) {
        for (int i = 1; i <= n; ++i) {
            int max_length = 0;
            for (int k = i; k > 0; --k) {
                max_length = max(max_length, trails[k - 1]);
                dp[i][j] = min(dp[i][j], dp[k - 1][j - 1] + max_length);
            }
        }
    }
    return dp[n][record];
}

import bisect

def main():
    input = sys.stdin.read
    data = input().split()
    
    N = int(data[0])
    Q = int(data[1])
    
    A = list(map(int, data[2:N+2]))
    queries = list(map(int, data[N+2:]))
    
    results = []
    
    for q in queries:
        # Use binary search to find the position
        pos = bisect.bisect_left(A, q)
        results.append(str(pos))
    
    # Output all results at once to minimize IO operations
    sys.stdout.write("\n".join(results) + "\n")

    main()

10/23/24, 19:33 - Manvi Joshi: def sum_of_regions(heights):
    n = len(heights)
    sum_regions = 0
    
    for i in range(n):
        left, right = i, i
        
        # Expand to the left
        while left > 0 and heights[left - 1] <= heights[i]:
            left -= 1
        
        # Expand to the right
        while right < n - 1 and heights[right + 1] <= heights[i]:
            right += 1
        
        # Region length for the current student
        region_length = right - left + 1
        sum_regions += region_length
    
    return sum_regions

10/23/24, 19:59 - Prachi Sah: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
using namespace std;

int computeTotalArea(vector<int>& studentHeights) {
    int totalArea = 0;
    int totalStudents = studentHeights.size();

    for (int idx = 0; idx < totalStudents; ++idx) {
        int leftBound = idx, rightBound = idx;

        // Expand left
        while (leftBound > 0 && studentHeights[leftBound - 1] <= studentHeights[idx]) {
            leftBound--;
        }

        // Expand right
        while (rightBound < totalStudents - 1 && studentHeights[rightBound + 1] <= studentHeights[idx]) {
            rightBound++;
        }

        // Calculate the length of the area
        int areaLength = rightBound - leftBound + 1;
        totalArea += areaLength;
    }

    return totalArea;
}

int main() {
    vector<int> studentHeights = {1, 2, 1}; // Sample input
    cout << computeTotalArea(studentHeights) << endl; // Output the result

}

10/23/24, 20:34 - Richarani: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <algorithm>
#include <limits>

int getUmbrellas(int requirement, std::vector<int>& sizes) {
    std::vector<int> dp(requirement + 1, std::numeric_limits<int>::max());
    dp[0] = 0; // No umbrellas needed for 0 people

    for (int size : sizes) {
        for (int j = size; j <= requirement; ++j) {
            if (dp[j - size] != std::numeric_limits<int>::max()) {
                dp[j] = std::min(dp[j], dp[j - size] + 1);
            }
        }
    }

    return dp[requirement] != std::numeric_limits<int>::max() ? dp[requirement] : -1;
}

int main() {
    int requirement = 5; // Example requirement
    std::vector<int> sizes = {1, 2, 3}; // Example sizes of umbrellas

    int result = getUmbrellas(requirement, sizes);
    std::cout << "Minimum umbrellas needed: " << result << std::endl;

    return 0;
}

10/23/24, 20:53 - GuğŸ’©: #include <iostream>
#include <cmath>
#include <string>
using namespace std;

int minOperationsToGoodString(string s) {
    int n = s.length();
    int moves = 0;

    // Traverse through the string
    for (int i = 1; i < n; i++) {
        // If current character doesn't match the previous one
        if (s[i] != s[i - 1]) {
            // Increment moves by the difference in character values
            moves += abs(s[i] - s[i - 1]);
            s[i] = s[i - 1]; // Make them equal by transforming current char
        }
    }

    // For the first and last characters, they need to be equal
    if (s[0] != s[n - 1]) {
        moves += abs(s[0] - s[n - 1]);
    }

    return moves;
}

int main() {
    string s = "abca";
    cout << "Minimum moves required: " << minOperationsToGoodString(s) << endl;
    return 0;
}
